              In the field of functional genomics, understanding how genes
              interact with each other in specific contexts is crucial for
              developing new therapies. However, current methods have
              limitations when it comes to analyzing complex traits that involve
              multiple genes working together. To address this gap, we introduce
              PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
              latent representation for a joint analysis. By grouping genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions, our method
              can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential
              targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our results show that
              diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
              in relevant cell types and that PhenoPLIER accurately predicts
              known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
              Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we
              find that functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Overall,
              PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic
              associations through the lens of gene modules and can help
              identify new therapeutic targets and drug repurposing
              opportunities.

              ---

              The field of complex trait research has been rapidly advancing in
              recent years, with transcriptome-wide association studies (TWAS)
              playing an important role in uncovering the role of individual
              genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of
              the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
              interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. This is where PhenoPLIER comes in: we introduce this
              novel computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis.


              PhenoPLIER's representation is based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions, allowing
              us to contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential
              targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our results show that
              diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
              in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, we
              find that functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER using a
              CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation.


              In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for
              interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene
              modules. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, we can
              contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets
              missed by single-gene strategies. This approach has significant
              broader significance for disease research, as it enables us to
              better understand how genes interact in specific contexts to
              perform their functions and ultimately develop new therapies.

              Genetic studies have long struggled to identify functional genes
              and their interactions in complex traits, hindering the
              development of new therapies. This manuscript presents a novel
              approach to address this challenge by leveraging gene expression
              patterns to identify gene modules associated with disease etiology

              algorithms to group co-expressed genes in specific contexts,
              allowing us to contextualize genetic associations and infer
              potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. We demonstrate
              the effectiveness of our approach through several examples,

              predicting known drug-disease pairs with high accuracy.

              important players in trait-associated modules, even when they lack
              direct associations. Overall, PhenoPLIER provides a powerful tool
              for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene
              modules, enabling us to better understand complex traits and
              develop more effective therapies.

            text: >-
              In recent years, the study of gene expression patterns has
              revolutionized our understanding of disease etiology and drug
              mechanisms. However, traditional approaches to genetic studies
              have limitations when it comes to analyzing complex traits that
              involve interactions between multiple genes. To address this
              challenge, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that
              leverages gene co-expression data to map gene-trait associations
              and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. Our approach is based on the
              idea that genes with similar expression patterns across different
              conditions are likely to be involved in the same biological
              processes. We demonstrate that PhenoPLIER accurately predicts
              known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action by
              analyzing disease associations with gene modules expressed in
              relevant cell types. Furthermore, we use a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation and find that functionally important
              players are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.
              Our results highlight the importance of functional genomics in
              identifying therapeutic targets for complex diseases and suggest
              that gene co-expression analysis can be used to predict drug
              repurposing. Overall, our study provides a valuable resource for
              researchers working on complex diseases and drug discovery.

              The field of functional genomics has revolutionized our
              understanding of how genes interact with each other and how they

              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for a joint analysis. This

              expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe that

              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our results
              highlight the importance of gene co-expression in understanding
              complex traits and suggest that drug repurposing strategies should
              be based on a clustering of disease mechanisms rather than
              individual genes.

            Genes act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform
            their functions. Determining how these genes influence complex
            traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation
            across different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is
            critical for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide

            in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the

            text: >-
              Genes work together in specific contexts to carry out their
              functions, and determining how these genes influence complex
              traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression
              regulation across different conditions. This insight is crucial
              for developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association
              studies have helped identify the role of individual genes in
              disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models predict that gene-gene
              interactions play a significant role in disease origin and
              progression. In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on
              modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions. We find that diseases are significantly associated
              with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
              approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
              mechanisms of action. Additionally, we use a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation and find that functionally important
              players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. Our findings highlight the importance of
              gene co-expression and clustering complex traits for disease
              etiology and drug mechanism discovery.

            text: >-
              The study of complex traits requires an understanding of how genes
              interact with each other and their expression patterns under
              different conditions. While transcriptome-wide association studies
              have been instrumental in identifying individual genes associated
              with disease mechanisms, the role of gene-gene interactions in
              disease etiology and drug mechanisms is not fully understood. This
              gap in knowledge hinders the development of new therapies for
              complex diseases. In this manuscript, we present PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that bridges this gap by mapping gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
              latent representation for joint analysis. Our method identifies
              modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions, which we show to be significantly associated with
              diseases in relevant cell types. Furthermore, PhenoPLIER
              accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms
              of action. We demonstrate the utility of PhenoPLIER by using a
              CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation and identifying
              functionally important players that lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules. Our findings provide
              insights into disease etiology and drug mechanisms, and highlight
              the potential for drug repurposing through clustering of complex
              traits.

            text: >-
              Genetic studies have been instrumental in identifying
              disease-relevant mechanisms, and functional genomics has provided
              insights into gene expression patterns across different
              conditions. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
              traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
              disease origin and progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for a joint analysis. This representation is based
              on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the
              same conditions. Our results show that diseases are significantly
              associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
              our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and
              infers mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important
              players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. These findings highlight the importance of
              gene co-expression patterns in disease etiology and drug
              mechanisms, and provide insights into therapeutic targets for
              complex traits.

              will fill. The first sentence orients the reader by introducing
              the broader field in which the manuscript's research is situated.
              Then, the context is narrowed until it lands on the open question
              that the research answers. A successful context section
              distinguishes the research’s contributions from the current
              state-of-the-art, communicating what is missing in the current
              literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e. the
              connection between the specific gap and the broader context). 2)
              The content portion (e.g. "here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that was used to fill the gap, then presents an
              executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion portion interprets
              the results to answer the question that was posed at the end of
              the context portion. There may be a second part to the conclusion
              portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the broader
              field forward (e.g. "broader significance").

              their functions. However, understanding how genes influence

              association studies have helped identify the role of individual
              genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. To address this challenge, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on
              modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions. We find that diseases are significantly associated

              approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
              mechanisms of action. Furthermore, we use a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation and find that functionally important
              players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. Overall, PhenoPLIER provides a powerful
              tool for identifying therapeutic targets and repurposing drugs
              based on gene expression patterns and disease etiology.

            text: >-
              The field of genetics has long recognized the importance of
              studying gene expression patterns in disease etiology and drug
              mechanisms. However, traditional approaches to gene expression
              analysis have been limited in their ability to capture complex
              interactions between genes and traits. In this study, we introduce
              PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that leverages functional
              genomics data to map gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
              analysis. By clustering genes with similar expression patterns
              across the same conditions, our method is able to identify modules
              of genes that play crucial roles in disease development and drug
              response. Our results demonstrate that diseases are significantly
              associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
              PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
              mechanisms of action. Furthermore, we use a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation and find that functionally important
              players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. Overall, our study highlights the
              importance of gene co-expression analysis in identifying
              therapeutic targets and drug repurposing for complex traits.
